1.1)">1.1</a></li></ul></li></ul></td>\n</tr></tbody></table>\n<p>An <b>HTML element</b> is a type of <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> (Hypertext Markup Language) document component, one of several types of HTML nodes (there are also text nodes, comment nodes and others).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness"><span title="This information is too vague. (February 2019)">vague</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> HTML document is composed of a <a href="/wiki/Tree_structure" title="Tree structure">tree</a> of simple HTML <a href="/wiki/Node_(computer_science)" title="Node (computer science)">nodes</a>, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Text_nodes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Text nodes (page does not exist)">text nodes</a>, and HTML elements, which add <a href="/wiki/Semantics" title="Semantics">semantics</a> and formatting to parts of document (e.g., make text bold, organize it into paragraphs, lists and tables, or embed <a href="/wiki/Hyperlink" title="Hyperlink">hyperlinks</a> and images). Each element can have <a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a> specified. Elements can also have content, including other elements and text.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concepts">Concepts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Concepts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Document_vs._DOM">Document vs. DOM</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Document vs. DOM">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>HTML documents are delivered as "documents".<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> These are then <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parsed</a>, which turns them into the <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">Document Object Model</a> (DOM) internal representation, within the web browser.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup> Presentation by the web browser (such as screen rendering or access by JavaScript) is then performed on this internal DOM, not the original document.\n</p><p>Early HTML documents (and to a lesser extent today\'s HTML documents) were largely <a href="/wiki/Invalid_HTML" class="mw-redirect" title="Invalid HTML">invalid HTML</a> and riddled with <a href="/wiki/Well-formed_HTML" class="mw-redirect" title="Well-formed HTML">syntax errors</a>. The parsing process was also required to "fix" these errors as best it could. The result was often not <em>correct</em> (i.e., it did not represent what a careless coder had originally intended) but was at least <a href="/wiki/Valid_HTML" class="mw-redirect" title="Valid HTML">valid</a> according to the HTML standard. Only in the rarest cases would the parser abandon parsing altogether.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elements_vs._tags">Elements vs. tags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Elements vs. tags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As is generally understood, the position of an element is indicated as spanning from a start tag, possibly including some child content, and is terminated by an end tag.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML401_Elements_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML401_Elements-6">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> This is the case for many, but not all, elements within an HTML document. The distinction is explicitly emphasised in <i>HTML 4.01 Specification</i>:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><b>Elements are not tags.</b> Some people refer to elements as tags (e.g., "the P tag"). Remember that the element is one thing, and the tag (be it start or end tag) is another. For instance, the HEAD element is always present, even though both start and end HEAD tags may be missing in the markup.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML401_Elements_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML401_Elements-6">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>\n<p>Similarly the W3C Recommendadtion <i><b>HTML 5.1 2nd Edition</b></i> explicitly says:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p><b>Tags</b> are used to delimit the start and end of elements in the markup. (...) The start and end tags of certain normal elements can be omitted, (...) <br /> The contents of the element must be placed between just after the start tag (which <u>might be implied</u>, in certain cases) and just before the end tag (which again, <u>might be implied</u>, in certain cases). </p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.w3.org/TR/html51/syntax.html#tags">HTML 5.1 2nd Edition \xc2\xa7 8.1.2. Elements \xc2\xa7 Tags</a></cite></div></blockquote>\n<p>and:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>\nCertain tags can be <b>omitted</b>. <br /> <b>NOTE:</b><br /> Omitting an element\'s start tag (...) does not mean the element is not present; it is implied, but it is still there. For example, an HTML document always has a root <kbd>&lt;html&gt;</kbd> element, even if the string <kbd>&lt;html&gt;</kbd> doesn\'t appear anywhere in the markup. </p><div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.w3.org/TR/html51/syntax.html#optional-tags">HTML 5.1 2nd Edition \xc2\xa7 8.1.2.4. Optional tags</a></cite></div></blockquote>\n<p><br />\nAs HTML (before HTML5) is based on <a href="/wiki/SGML" class="mw-redirect" title="SGML">SGML</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> its parsing also depends on the <a href="/wiki/Document_Type_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Document Type Definition">Document Type Definition (DTD)</a>, specifically an HTML DTD (e.g. HTML 4.01<sup id="cite_ref-W3C,_HTML_401_DTD_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C,_HTML_401_DTD-8">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;note 4&#93;</a></sup>). The DTD specifies which element types are possible (i.e. it defines the set of element types) and also the valid combinations in which they may appear in a document. It is part of general SGML behavior that, where only one valid structure is <em>possible</em> (per the DTD), its explicit statement in any given document is not generally required. As a simple example, the <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> tag indicating the start of a paragraph element should be complemented by a <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> tag indicating its end. But since the DTD states that paragraph elements cannot be nested, an HTML document fragment <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 1 <span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 2 <span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 3</code>is thus inferred to be equivalent to <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 1 <span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 2 <span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Para 3</code>. (If one paragraph element cannot contain another, any currently open paragraph must be closed before starting another.) Because this implication is based on the combination of the DTD and the individual document, it is not usually possible to infer elements from document tags <em>alone</em> but only by using an SGML\xe2\x80\x94or HTML\xe2\x80\x94aware parser with knowledge of the DTD. <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> creates a similar result by defining what tags can be omitted.<sup id="cite_ref-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SGML_vs._XML">SGML vs. XML</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: SGML vs. XML">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>SGML is complex, which has limited its widespread understanding and adoption. <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> was developed as a simpler alternative. Although both can use the DTD to specify the supported elements and their permitted combinations as document structure, XML parsing is simpler. The relation from tags to elements is always that of parsing the actual tags included in the document, without the implied closures that are part of SGML.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;note 5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>HTML as used on the current web is likely to be either treated as XML, by being <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>, or as <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>; in either case the parsing of document tags into DOM elements is simplified compared to legacy HTML systems. Once the DOM of elements is obtained, behavior at higher levels of interface (example: screen rendering) is identical or nearly so.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;note 6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".25block.3B_vs._box"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="%block;_vs._box"><code>%block;</code> vs. box</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: %block; vs. box">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Part of this CSS presentation behavior is the notion of the "<a href="/wiki/CSS_box_model" title="CSS box model">box model</a>". This is applied to those elements that CSS considers to be "block" elements, set through the CSS <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="nt">display</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nt">block</span><span class="o">;</span></code> declaration.\n</p><p>HTML also has a similar concept, although different, and the two are very frequently confused. <code>%block;</code> and <code>%inline;</code> are groups within the HTML DTD that group elements as being either "block-level" or "inline".<sup id="cite_ref-W3C,_HTML_4.01,_block_and_inline_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C,_HTML_4.01,_block_and_inline-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> This is used to define their nesting behavior: block-level elements cannot be placed into an inline context.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;note 7&#93;</a></sup> This behavior cannot be changed; it is fixed in the DTD. Block and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Inline_elements&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Inline elements (page does not exist)">inline elements</a> have the appropriate and different <a href="/wiki/CSS" title="CSS">CSS</a> behaviors attached to them by default,<sup id="cite_ref-W3C,_HTML_4.01,_block_and_inline_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C,_HTML_4.01,_block_and_inline-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> including the relevance of the box model for particular element types.\n</p><p>Note though that this CSS behavior can, and frequently is, changed from the default. Lists with <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">ul</span><span class="p">&gt;&lt;</span><span class="nt">li</span><span class="p">&gt;</span> ...</code> are <code>%block;</code> elements and are presented as block elements by default. However, it is quite common to set these with CSS to display as an inline list.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">Syntax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Syntax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:fit-content; width:-moz-fit-content; width:-webkit-fit-content;"><div                       <mo mathvariant="monospace">&gt;</mo>\n                        </mstyle>\n                      </mrow>\n                      <mo>&#x23DE;<!-- \xe2\x8f\x9e --></mo>\n                    </mover>\n                  </mrow>\n                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                      <mfrac linethickness="0">\n                        <mrow>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">E</mi>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">n</mi>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">d</mi>\n                        </mrow>\n                        <mrow>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">t</mi>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">a</mi>\n                          <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">g</mi>\n                        </mrow>\n                      </mfrac>\n                    </mrow>\n                  </mrow>\n                </mover>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>&#x23DE;<!-- \xe2\x8f\x9e --></mo>\n            </mover>\n          </mrow>\n          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">E</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">l</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">e</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">m</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">e</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">n</mi>\n              <mi mathvariant="sans-serif">t</mi>\n            </mrow>\n          </mrow>\n        </mover>\n      </mstyle>\n    </mrow>\n    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\overbrace {\\overbrace {{\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&lt;\\!p\\ }}\\color {Magenta}\\underbrace {\\mathtt {class}} _{\\mathsf {\\color {Black}{Attribute \\atop name}}}{\\mathtt {=\'\'}}\\!\\underbrace {\\mathtt {paragraph}} _{\\mathsf {\\color {White}{Attr} \\atop \\color {Black}Attribute\\ value}}\'\'{\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&gt;}}} ^{\\mathsf {Start\\ tag}}\\overbrace {\\mathtt {\\color {Green}This\\ is\\ a\\ paragraph.}} ^{\\mathsf {Content}}\\overbrace {\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&lt;\\!/p\\!&gt;}} ^{\\mathsf {End \\atop tag}}} ^{\\mathsf {Element}}}</annotation>\n  </semantics>\n</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/37506127f0730d9b6035530f46c706af4e2319d4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -5.338ex; margin-right: -0.028ex; width:55.167ex; height:15.009ex;" alt="{\\displaystyle \\overbrace {\\overbrace {{\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&lt;\\!p\\ }}\\color {Magenta}\\underbrace {\\mathtt {class}} _{\\mathsf {\\color {Black}{Attribute \\atop name}}}{\\mathtt {=&#039;&#039;}}\\!\\underbrace {\\mathtt {paragraph}} _{\\mathsf {\\color {White}{Attr} \\atop \\color {Black}Attribute\\ value}}&#039;&#039;{\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&gt;}}} ^{\\mathsf {Start\\ tag}}\\overbrace {\\mathtt {\\color {Green}This\\ is\\ a\\ paragraph.}} ^{\\mathsf {Content}}\\overbrace {\\mathtt {\\color {BrickRed}&lt;\\!/p\\!&gt;}} ^{\\mathsf {End \\atop tag}}} ^{\\mathsf {Element}}}"/></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Parts of an HTML container element</div></div></div>\n<p>In the HTML syntax, most elements are written with a start tag and an end tag, with the content in between. An <b>HTML tag</b> is composed of the name of the element, surrounded by <a href="/wiki/Angle_bracket" class="mw-redirect" title="Angle bracket">angle brackets</a>. An end tag also has a slash after the opening angle bracket, to distinguish it from the start tag. For example, a paragraph, which is represented by the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;p&gt;</code> element, would be written as:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>In the HTML syntax, most elements are written ...<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>However, not all of these elements <em>require</em> the end tag, or even the start tag, to be present.<sup id="cite_ref-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>  Some elements, the so-called <i><a href="#Void_elements">void elements</a></i>, do not have an end tag. A typical example is the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;br&gt;</code> (hard line-break) element. A void element\'s behavior is predefined, and it cannot contain any content or other elements. For example, an address would be written as:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>P. Sherman<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">br</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>42 Wallaby Way<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">br</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Sydney<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>When using <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>, it is required to open and close all elements, including void elements. This can be done by placing an end tag immediately after the start tag, but this is not legal in HTML 5 and will lead to two elements being created. An alternative way to specify that it is a void element, which is compatible with both XHTML and HTML 5, is to put a <code> /</code> at the <em>end</em> of the tag (not to be confused with the <code>/</code> at the <em>beginning</em> of a closing tag).\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>P. Sherman<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">br</span> <span class="p">/&gt;</span>42 Wallaby Way<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">br</span> <span class="p">/&gt;</span>Sydney<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">p</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a> are specified inside the start tag. For example, the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;abbr&gt;</code> element, which represents an <a href="/wiki/Abbreviation" title="Abbreviation">abbreviation</a>, expects a <code>title</code> attribute within its opening tag. This would be written as:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">abbr</span> <span class="na">title</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;abbreviation&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>abbr.<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">abbr</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>There are multiple kinds of <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> elements: void elements, raw text elements, and normal elements.\n</p><p><b><span class="anchor" id="Empty_element"></span><span id="Void_elements">Void elements</span></b> (also sometimes called empty elements, single elements or stand-alone elements) only have a start tag (in the form <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&gt;</code>), which contains any <a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a>. They may not contain any children, such as text or other elements. For compatibility with <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>, the HTML specification allows an optional space and slash (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> is permissible). The space and slash are required in <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> and other <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> applications. Two common void elements are <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;br&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> (for a <a href="/wiki/Hard_return" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard return">hard line-break</a>, such as in a poem or an address) and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;hr&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> (for a thematic break). Other such elements are often place-holders which reference external files, such as the image (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;img&#32;&#47;&gt;</code>) element. The attributes included in the element will then point to the external file in question. Another example of a void element is <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;link&#32;&#47;&gt;</code>, for which the syntax is:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">link</span> <span class="na">rel</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;stylesheet&quot;</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;fancy.css&quot;</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;text/css&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>This <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;link&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> element points the browser at a <a href="/wiki/Style_sheet_(web_development)" title="Style sheet (web development)">style sheet</a> to use when presenting the HTML document to the user. Note that in the HTML syntax attributes don\'t have to be quoted if they are composed only of certain characters: letters, digits, the hyphen-minus and the period. When using the XML syntax (XHTML), on the other hand, all attributes must be quoted, and a spaced trailing <a href="/wiki/Slash_(punctuation)" title="Slash (punctuation)">slash</a> is required before the last angle bracket:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-xml mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="nt">&lt;link</span> <span class="na">rel=</span><span class="s">&quot;stylesheet&quot;</span> <span class="na">href=</span><span class="s">&quot;fancy.css&quot;</span> <span class="na">type=</span><span class="s">&quot;text/css&quot;</span> <span class="nt">/&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p><b><span id="Raw_text_elements">Raw text elements</span></b> (also known as text or text-only elements) are constructed with:\n</p>\n<ul><li>a <i>start tag</i> (in the form <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&gt;</code>) marking the beginning of an element, which may incorporate any number of <a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a>;</li>\n<li>some amount of text <i>content</i>, but no elements (all tags, apart from the applicable end tag, will be interpreted as content);</li>\n<li>an <i>end tag</i>, in which the element name is prefixed with a slash: <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;&#47;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&gt;</code>. In some versions of HTML, the end tag is optional for some elements. The end tag is required in <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>An example is the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;title&gt;</code> element must not contain other elements (including markup of text), only <em>plain</em> text.\n</p><p><b><span id="Normal_elements">Normal elements</span></b> usually have both a start tag and an end tag, although for some elements the end tag, or both tags, can be omitted. It is constructed in a similar way:\n</p>\n<ul><li>a <i>start tag</i> (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&gt;</code>) marking the beginning of an element, which may incorporate any number of <a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a>;</li>\n<li>some amount of <i>content</i>, including text and other elements;</li>\n<li>an <i>end tag</i>, in which the element name is prefixed with a <a href="/wiki/Slash_(punctuation)" title="Slash (punctuation)">slash</a>: <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;&#47;<var style="padding-right: 1px;">tag</var>&gt;</code>.</li></ul>\n<p><b><a href="/wiki/HTML_attribute" title="HTML attribute">HTML attributes</a></b> define desired behavior or indicate additional element properties. Most attributes require a <i>value</i>. In HTML, the value can be left unquoted if it does not include spaces (<code><var style="padding-right: 1px;">attribute</var>=<var style="padding-right: 1px;">value</var></code>), or it can be quoted with single or double quotes (<code><var style="padding-right: 1px;">attribute</var>=\'<var style="padding-right: 1px;">value</var>\'</code> or <code><var style="padding-right: 1px;">attribute</var>="<var style="padding-right: 1px;">value</var>"</code>). In <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>, those quotes are required.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Boolean_data_type" title="Boolean data type">Boolean</a> attributes, on the other hand, don\'t require a value to be specified. An example is the <code>checked</code> for checkboxes:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">input</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">checkbox</span> <span class="na">checked</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>In the XML (and thus <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>) syntax, though, the name should be repeated as the value:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-xml mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr"><pre><span></span><span class="nt">&lt;input</span> <span class="na">type=</span><span class="s">&quot;checkbox&quot;</span> <span class="na">checked=</span><span class="s">&quot;checked&quot;</span> <span class="nt">/&gt;</span>\n</pre></div>\n<p>Informally, HTML elements are sometimes referred to as "tags" (an example of <a href="/wiki/Synecdoche" title="Synecdoche">synecdoche</a>), though many prefer the term <i>tag</i> strictly in reference to the markup delimiting the start and end of an element.\n</p><p>Element (and attribute) names may be written in any combination of upper or lower case in HTML, but must be in lower case in XHTML.<sup id="cite_ref-XHTML10-42_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHTML10-42-17">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The canonical form was upper-case until <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, and was used in HTML specifications, but in recent years, lower-case has become more common.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Element_standards">Element standards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Element standards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>HTML elements are defined in a series of freely available open standards issued since 1995, initially by the <a href="/wiki/IETF" class="mw-redirect" title="IETF">IETF</a> and subsequently by the <a href="/wiki/W3C" class="mw-redirect" title="W3C">W3C</a>.\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Browser_wars" title="Browser wars">browser wars</a> of the 1990s, developers of <a href="/wiki/User_agent" title="User agent">user agents</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Web_browser" title="Web browser">web browsers</a>) often developed their own elements, some of which have been adopted in later standards. Other user agents may not recognize non-standard elements, and they will be ignored, possibly causing the page to be displayed improperly.\n</p><p>In 1998, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> (a simplified form of SGML) introduced mechanisms to allow anyone to develop their own elements and incorporate them in <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> documents, for use with XML-aware user agents.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Subsequently, HTML 4.01 was rewritten in an <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a>-compatible form, <a href="#XHTML10">XHTML 1.0</a> (<i>eXtensible HTML</i>). The elements in each are identical, and in most cases valid <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> 1.0 documents will be valid or nearly valid HTML 4.01 documents. This article mainly focuses on real HTML, unless noted otherwise; however, it remains applicable to <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>. See <a href="/wiki/HTML#SGML-based_versus_XML-based_HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> for a discussion of the minor differences between the two.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Element_status">Element status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Element status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since the first version of HTML, several elements have become outmoded, and are <i><a href="/wiki/Deprecated" class="mw-redirect" title="Deprecated">deprecated</a></i> in later standards, or do not appear at all, in which case they are <i>invalid</i> (and will be found invalid, and perhaps not displayed, by <a href="/wiki/XML_validation" title="XML validation">validating</a> user agents).<sup id="cite_ref-XML10-51_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XML10-51-19">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4.01" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4.01">HTML 4.01</a> / <a href="/wiki/XHTML_1.0" class="mw-redirect" title="XHTML 1.0">XHTML 1.0</a>, the status of elements is complicated by the existence of three types of <a href="/wiki/Document_Type_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Document Type Definition">DTD</a>:\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Transitional</b>, which contain deprecated elements, but which were intended to provide a transitional period during which authors could update their practices;</li>\n<li><b>Frameset</b>, which are versions of the Transitional DTDs which also allow authors to write <b>frameset</b> documents;</li>\n<li><b>Strict</b>, which is the up-to-date (as at 1999) form of HTML.</li></ul>\n<p>HTML5 instead provides a listing of <b>obsolete</b> features to go along with the <b>standardized</b> normative content. They are broken down into "obsolete but conforming" for which implementation instructions exist and "non-conforming" ones that should be replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first Standard (<a href="/wiki/HTML#First_specifications" title="HTML">HTML 2.0</a>) contained four deprecated elements, one of which was invalid in <a href="/wiki/HTML_3.2" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 3.2">HTML 3.2</a>. All four are invalid in <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4.01 Transitional</a>, which also deprecated a further ten elements. All of these, plus two others, are invalid in <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4.01 Strict</a>. While the frame elements are still current in the sense of being present in the Transitional and Frameset DTDs, there are no plans to preserve them in future standards, as their function has been largely replaced, and they are highly problematic for user accessibility.\n</p><p>(Strictly speaking, the most recent <i>XHTML</i> standard, <a href="/wiki/XHTML_1.1" class="mw-redirect" title="XHTML 1.1">XHTML 1.1</a> (2001), does not include frames at all; it is approximately equivalent to <a href="/wiki/XHTML_1.0" class="mw-redirect" title="XHTML 1.0">XHTML 1.0 Strict</a>, but also includes the <b><a href="/wiki/Ruby_(annotation_markup)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruby (annotation markup)">Ruby markup</a></b> module.)<sup id="cite_ref-XHTML11_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-XHTML11-21">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A common source of confusion is the loose use of <i>deprecated</i> to refer to both deprecated and invalid status, and to elements that are expected to be formally deprecated in the future.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Content_vs._presentation_and_behavior">Content vs. presentation and behavior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Content vs. presentation and behavior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since HTML 4, HTML has increasingly focused on the separation of content (the visible text and images) from presentation (like color, font size, and layout).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  This is often referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_concerns" title="Separation of concerns">separation of concerns</a>. HTML is used to represent the structure or content of a document, its presentation remains the sole responsibility of <a href="/wiki/CSS" title="CSS">CSS</a> <a href="/wiki/Style_sheet_(web_development)" title="Style sheet (web development)">style sheets</a>. A default style sheet is suggested as part of the CSS standard, giving a default rendering for HTML.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Behavior (interactivity) is also kept separate from content, and is handled by <a href="/wiki/Client-side_scripting" class="mw-redirect" title="Client-side scripting">scripts</a>. Images are contained in separate <a href="/wiki/Graphics" title="Graphics">graphics</a> files, separate from text, though they can also be considered part of the content of a page.\n</p><p>Separation of concerns allows the document to be presented by different user agents according to their purposes and abilities. For example, a user agent can select an appropriate style sheet to present a document by displaying on a monitor, printing on paper, or to determine speech characteristics in an audio-only user agent. The structural and semantic functions of the markup remain identical in each case.\n</p><p>Historically, user agents did not always support these features. In the 1990s, as a stop-gap, presentational elements (like <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;b&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;i&gt;</code>) were added to HTML, at the cost of creating problems for interoperability and user accessibility. This is now regarded as outmoded and has been superseded by style sheet-based design; most presentational elements are now deprecated.<sup id="cite_ref-HTML401-141_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HTML401-141-24">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>External image files are incorporated with the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;img&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;object&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> elements. (With <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Scalable_Vector_Graphics" title="Scalable Vector Graphics">SVG</a> language can also be used to write graphics within the document, though linking to external SVG files is generally simpler.)<sup id="cite_ref-SVG11-23_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SVG11-23-25">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Where an image is not purely decorative, HTML allows replacement content with similar semantic value to be provided for non-visual user agents.\n</p><p>An HTML document can also be extended through the use of scripts to provide additional behaviors beyond the abilities of HTML hyperlinks and forms.\n</p><p>The elements <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;style&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&gt;</code>, with related <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a>, provide style sheets and scripts.\n</p>\n<ul><li>In the document head, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;style&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> may link to shared external documents, or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;style&gt;...&lt;&#47;style&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&gt;...&lt;&#47;script&gt;</code> may contain embedded instructions. (The <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;link&gt;</code> element can also be used to link style sheets.)</li>\n<li><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&gt;...&lt;&#47;script&gt;</code> can occur at any point in the document (head or body).</li>\n<li>The <code>style</code> attribute is valid in most document body elements (e.g. <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;div&#32;style="..."&gt;</code>) for inclusion of <i>inline style</i> instructions.</li>\n<li><i>Event-handling attributes</i>, which provide links to scripts, are optional in most elements.</li>\n<li>For user agents which do not operate scripts, the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;noscript&gt;...&lt;&#47;noscript&gt;</code> element provides embedded alternative content where appropriate; however, it can only be used in the document head and in the body as a block-level element.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Document_structure_elements">Document structure elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Document structure elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="html"></span><span class="anchor" id="html_tag"></span><code class="html" title="HTML" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;html</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/html&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>The <a href="/wiki/Root_element" title="Root element">root element</a> of an <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> document; all other elements are contained in this.</dd>\n<dd>The HTML element delimits the beginning and the end of an HTML document.</dd>\n<dd>Both the start and end tags may be omitted (HTML5).<sup id="cite_ref-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="head"></span><span class="anchor" id="head_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Head" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;head</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/head&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Container for processing information and metadata for an HTML document.</dd>\n<dd>Both the start and end tags may be omitted and inferred from child elements (HTML5).<sup id="cite_ref-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd>\n<dd>(See <a href="#Document_head_elements">document head elements</a> for child elements.)</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="body"></span><span class="anchor" id="body_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Body" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;body</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/body&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Container for the displayable content of an HTML document.</dd>\n<dd>Both the start and end tags may be omitted and inferred from child elements (HTML5).<sup id="cite_ref-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-whatwg-syntax-tag-omission-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd>\n<dd>(See <a href="#Document_body_elements">document body elements</a> for child elements.)</dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Document_head_elements">Document head elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Document head elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="base"></span><span class="anchor" id="base_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Base" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;base</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Specifies a <b>base URL</b> for all relative <code>href</code> and other links in the document. Must appear before any element that refers to an external resource. HTML permits only one <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;base&gt;</code> element for each document. This element has <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a>, but no contents.</dd>\n<dd>A development version of this element (as <code>BASE</code>) is mentioned in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>; <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="basefont"></span><span class="anchor" id="basefont_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Base Font" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;basefont</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Specifies a base font size, typeface, and color for the document. Used together with <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;font&gt;</code> elements. <a href="/wiki/Deprecation" title="Deprecation">Deprecated</a> in favor of <a href="/wiki/Style_sheet_(web_development)" title="Style sheet (web development)">style sheets</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a>; <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="isindex"></span><span class="anchor" id="isindex_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Index" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;isindex</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">isindex</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> could either appear in the document head or in the body, but only once in a document. See <a href="/wiki/Fieldset" class="mw-redirect" title="Fieldset">Forms</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="link"></span><span class="anchor" id="link_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Link" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;link</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Specifies links to other documents, such as <i>previous</i> and <i>next</i> links, or alternate versions.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  A common use is to link to external <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">style sheets</a>, using the form:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">link</span> <span class="na">rel</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;stylesheet&quot;</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;text/css&quot;</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;url&quot;</span> <span class="na">title</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;description_of_style&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>A less-common, but important, usage is to supply navigation hints consistently through use of <a href="/wiki/Microformat" title="Microformat">microformats</a>. Several common relationships are defined, that may be exposed to users through the browser interface rather than directly in the web page.\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">link</span> <span class="na">rel</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;next&quot;</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;url&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>A document\'s <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;head&gt;</code> element may contain any number of <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;link&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> elements. This element has <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a>, but no contents.</dd>\n<dd><code>LINK</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="meta"></span><span class="anchor" id="meta_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Meta" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;meta</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Meta_element" title="Meta element">Meta element</a></div>\n<dl><dd>Can be used to specify additional <a href="/wiki/Metadata" title="Metadata">metadata</a> about a document, such as its author, publication date, expiration date, language, page title, page description, keywords, or other information not provided through the other header elements and <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a>. Because of their generic nature, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> elements specify associative <a href="/wiki/Associative_array" title="Associative array">key-value pairs</a>. In general, a meta element conveys hidden information about the document. Several meta tags can be used, all of which should be nested in the head element. The specific purpose of each <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> element is defined by its attributes. Outside of <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a>, it is often given without the slash (<code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&gt;</code>), despite being a <a href="#Void_elements">void element</a>.</dd>\n<dd>In one form, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> elements can specify <a href="/wiki/HTTP" class="mw-redirect" title="HTTP">HTTP</a> headers which should be sent by a <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">web server</a> before the actual content. For example, <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">meta</span> <span class="na">http-equiv</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;foo&quot;</span> <span class="na">content</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;bar&quot;</span> <span class="p">/&gt;</span></code> specifies that the page should be served with an HTTP header called <code>foo</code> that has a value <code>bar</code>.</dd>\n<dd>In the general form, a <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> element specifies <code>name</code> and associated <code>content</code> <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a> describing aspects of the HTML page. To prevent possible ambiguity, an optional third attribute, <code>scheme</code>, may be supplied to specify a semantic framework that defines the meaning of the key and its value. For example, in <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">meta</span> <span class="na">name</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;foo&quot;</span> <span class="na">content</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;bar&quot;</span> <span class="na">scheme</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;DC&quot;</span> <span class="p">/&gt;</span></code> the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;meta&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> element identifies itself as containing the <code>foo</code> element, with a value of <code>bar</code>, from the DC or <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Core" title="Dublin Core">Dublin Core</a> <a href="/wiki/Resource_Description_Framework" title="Resource Description Framework">resource description framework</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="object"></span><code class="html" title="Object" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;object</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/object&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used for including generic objects within the document header. Though rarely used within a <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;head&gt;</code> element, it could potentially be used to extract foreign data and associate it with the current document.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="script"></span><span class="anchor" id="script_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Script" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;script</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/script&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Can act as a container for script instructions or link to an external script with the optional <code>src</code> attribute.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Also usable in the document body to dynamically generate either both block or inline content.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="style"></span><span class="anchor" id="style_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Style" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;style</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/style&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Specifies a <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">style</a> for the document, usually in the form:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">style</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;text/css&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span> <span class="o">...</span> <span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">style</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>Can either act as a container for style instructions or link to external style sheets \xe2\x80\x93 for example, in <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a>, with <code>@import</code> directives of the form:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">style</span><span class="p">&gt;</span> <span class="p">@</span><span class="k">import</span> <span class="nt">url</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">style</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="title"></span><span class="anchor" id="title_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Title" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;title</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/title&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>This tag defines a document title. Required in every <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> and <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> document. User agents may use the title in different ways. For example:\n<ul><li>Web browsers usually display it in a window\'s <a href="/wiki/Title_bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Title bar">title bar</a> when the window is open, and (where applicable) in the <a href="/wiki/Task_bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Task bar">task bar</a> when the window is minimized.</li>\n<li>It may become the default file-name when saving the page.</li>\n<li>We can use &lt;title&gt; element only one time in a web page, and when we make another page then we will use again another &lt;title&gt; element with new title (don\'t take same name for all title tag in website, It can be problem for search engines).</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" class="mw-redirect" title="Web search engine">Web search engines</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Web_crawler" title="Web crawler">web crawlers</a> may pay particular attention to the words used in the title.</li></ul></dd>\n<dd>The <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;title&gt;</code> element must not contain other elements, only text. Only one  <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;title&gt;</code> element is permitted in a document.</dd>\n<dd>Existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Document_body_elements">Document body elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Document body elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In visual browsers, displayable elements can be rendered as either <i>block</i> or <i>inline</i>. While all elements are part of the document sequence, block elements appear within their parent elements:\n</p>\n<ul><li>as rectangular objects which do not break across lines;</li>\n<li>with block margins, width and height properties which can be set independently of the surrounding elements.</li></ul>\n<p>Conversely, inline elements are treated as part of the flow of document text; they cannot have margins, width or height set, and do break across lines.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Block_elements">Block elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Block elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Block elements, or block-level elements, have a rectangular structure. By default, these elements will span the entire width of its parent element, and will thus not allow any other element to occupy the same horizontal space as it is placed on.\n</p><p>The rectangular structure of a block element is often referred to as the <a href="/wiki/File:W3C_and_Internet_Explorer_box_models.svg" title="File:W3C and Internet Explorer box models.svg">box model</a>, and is made up of several parts. Each element contains the following:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <b>content</b> of an element is the actual text (or other media) placed between the opening and closing tags of an element.</li>\n<li>The <b>padding</b> of an element is the space around the content but which still forms part of the element. Padding should not be used to create white space between two elements. Any background style assigned to the element, such as a background image or color, will be visible within the padding. Increasing the size of an element\'s padding increases the amount of space this element will take up.</li>\n<li>The <b>border</b> of an element is the absolute end of an element, and spans the perimeter of that element. The thickness of a border increases the size of an element.</li>\n<li>The <b>margin</b> of an element is the white-space that surrounds an element. The content, padding and border of any other element will not be allowed to enter this area, unless forced to do so by some advanced <a href="/wiki/CSS" title="CSS">CSS</a> placement. Using most standard <a href="/wiki/Document_Type_Definition" class="mw-redirect" title="Document Type Definition">DTDs</a>, margins on the left and right of different elements will push each other away. Margins on the top or bottom of an element, on the other hand, will not stack, or will intermingle. This means that the white-space between these elements will be as big as the larger margin between them.</li></ul>\n<p>The above section refers only to the detailed implementation of CSS rendering and has no relevance to HTML elements themselves.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Basic_text">Basic text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Basic text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="p"></span><span class="anchor" id="p_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Paragraph" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;p</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/p&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Creates a paragraph, perhaps the most common block level element.</dd>\n<dd><code>P</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="heading"></span><span class="anchor" id="h1"></span><span class="anchor" id="h1_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Primary Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h1</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h1&gt;</b>\n</code>\n<span class="anchor" id="h2"></span><span class="anchor" id="h2_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Secondary Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h2</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h2&gt;</b>\n</code>\n<span class="anchor" id="h3"></span><span class="anchor" id="h3_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Third Level Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h3</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h3&gt;</b>\n</code>\n<span class="anchor" id="h4"></span><span class="anchor" id="h4_tag"></span><code class="html" title="4. Level Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h4</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h4&gt;</b>\n</code>\n<span class="anchor" id="h5"></span><span class="anchor" id="h5_tag"></span><code class="html" title="5. Level Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h5</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h5&gt;</b>\n</code>\n<span class="anchor" id="h6"></span><span class="anchor" id="h6_tag"></span><code class="html" title="6. Level Headline" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;h6</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/h6&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Section headings at different levels. <code>h1</code> delimits the highest-level heading, <code>h2</code> the next level down (sub-section), <code>h3</code> for a level below that, and so on to <code>h6</code>. They are sometimes referred to collectively as <code>h<i>n</i></code> tags, <i>n</i> meaning any of the available heading levels.</dd>\n<dd>Most visual browsers show headings as large bold text by default, though this can be overridden with <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">CSS</a>. Heading elements are not intended merely for creating large or bold text \xe2\x80\x93 in fact, they should <em>not</em> be used for explicitly styling text. Rather, they describe the document\'s structure and organization. Some programs use them to generate outlines and tables of contents.</dd>\n<dd>Headings existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and were <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lists">Lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="dl"></span><span class="anchor" id="dl_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Definition List" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;dl</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/dl&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Definition list" redirects here. For Wikipedia\'s article on lists of definitions, see <a href="/wiki/Glossary" title="Glossary">Glossary</a>.</div>\n<dl><dd>A description list (a.k.a. <a href="/wiki/Association_list" title="Association list">association list</a> or definition list), which consists of name\xe2\x80\x93value groups,<sup id="cite_ref-W3C-5-DL_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W3C-5-DL-30">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and was known as a definition list prior to HTML5.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  Description lists are intended for groups of "terms and definitions, metadata topics and values, questions and answers, or any other groups of name\xe2\x80\x93value data".<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><code>DL</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="dt"></span><span class="anchor" id="dt_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Definition Term" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;dt</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/dt&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A name in a description list (previously definition term in a definition list).</dd>\n<dd><code>DT</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="dd"></span><span class="anchor" id="dd_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Definition" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;dd</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/dd&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A value in a description list (previously definition data in a definition list).</dd>\n<dd><code>DD</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="ol"></span><span class="anchor" id="ol_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ordered List" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;ol</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/ol&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dd>An ordered (enumerated) list. The <code>type</code> attribute can be used to specify the kind of marker to use in the list, but style sheets give more control. The default is Arabic numbering.  In an HTML attribute: <span class="nowrap"><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">ol</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;foo&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></span>; or in a CSS declaration: <span class="nowrap"><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="nt">ol</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">list-style-type</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="n">foo</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></span> \xe2\x80\x93 replacing <code><var>foo</var></code> with one of the following:\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Style</th>\n<th>HTML value</th>\n<th>CSS value\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>A, B, C&#160;...</td>\n<td><code>A</code></td>\n<td><code>upper-alpha</code>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>a, b, c&#160;...</td>\n<td><code>a</code></td>\n<td><code>lower-alpha</code>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>I, II, III&#160;...</td>\n<td><code>I</code></td>\n<td><code>upper-roman</code>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>i, ii, iii&#160;...</td>\n<td><code>i</code></td>\n<td><code>lower-roman</code>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1, 2, 3&#160;...</td>\n<td><code>1</code></td>\n<td><code>decimal</code>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>CSS provides several other options not available as pure-HTML markup, including <code>none</code>, and options for <a href="/wiki/CJK" class="mw-redirect" title="CJK">CJK</a>, Hebrew, Georgian, and Armenian script.\n</p>\n</dd>\n<dl><dd><code>OL</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n\n<p><span class="anchor" id="ul"></span><span class="anchor" id="ul_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Unordered List" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;ul</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/ul&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p><dl><dd>An unordered (bulleted) list. The type of list item marker can be specified in an HTML attribute: <span class="nowrap"><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">ul</span> <span class="na">type</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;foo&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></span>; or in a CSS declaration: <span class="nowrap"><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="nt">ul</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">list-style-type</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="n">foo</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></span> \xe2\x80\x93 replacing <code><var>foo</var></code> with one of the following (the same values are used in HTML and CSS): <code>disc</code> (the default), <code>square</code>, or <code>circle</code>. <b>Only</b> the CSS method is supported in HTML5. CSS also provides <code>none</code>, and the ability to replace these bullets with custom images.</dd>\n<dd><code>UL</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n\n<p><span class="anchor" id="li"></span><span class="anchor" id="li_tag"></span><code class="html" title="List Item" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;li</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/li&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p><dl><dd>A list item in ordered (<code>ol</code>) or unordered (<code>ul</code>) lists.</dd>\n<dd><code>LI</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n\n<p><span class="anchor" id="dir"></span><span class="anchor" id="dir_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Directory List" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;dir</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/dir&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p><dl><dd>A directory listing. The original purpose of this element was never widely supported; deprecated in favor of <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">ul</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code>.</dd>\n<dd><code>DIR</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a>; <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>.</dd></dl>\n\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_block_elements">Other block elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Other block elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="address"></span><span class="anchor" id="address_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Address" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;address</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/address&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Contact information for the document author.</dd>\n<dd><code>ADDRESS</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="article"></span><span class="anchor" id="article_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Article" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;article</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/article&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Article_element" title="Article element">Article element</a></div>\n<dl><dd>Used for articles and other similar content.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="aside"></span><span class="anchor" id="aside_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Aside" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;aside</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/aside&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used for content in a document which is separate from the main page content, for example, sidebars or advertising.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="blockquote"></span> \n<span class="anchor" id="blockquote"></span><span class="anchor" id="blockquote_tag"></span><code class="html" title="BlockQuotation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;blockquote</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/blockquote&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blockquote_element" title="Blockquote element">Blockquote element</a></div>\n<dl><dd>A <a href="/wiki/Blockquote" class="mw-redirect" title="Blockquote">block level quotation</a>, for when the quotation includes block level elements, e.g. paragraphs. The <code>cite</code> attribute (not to be confused with the <a href="#cite"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;cite&gt;</code></a> element) may give the source, and must be a fully qualified <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Identifier" title="Uniform Resource Identifier">Uniform Resource Identifier</a>.</dd>\n<dd>The default presentation of block quotations in visual browsers is usually to indent them from both margins. This has led to the element being unnecessarily used just to indent paragraphs, regardless of semantics. For quotations not containing block level elements see the quote (<a href="#q"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;q&gt;</code></a>) element.</dd>\n<dd><code>BLOCKQUOTE</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current. See <a href="/wiki/Blockquote_element" title="Blockquote element">blockquote element</a> for more information.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="center"></span><span class="anchor" id="center_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Centered Text" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;center</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/center&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Creates a block-level center-aligned division. Deprecated in favor of <a href="#div"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;div&gt;</code></a> or another element with centering defined using style sheets.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; <b>not supported</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="del"></span><span class="anchor" id="del_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Deleted Section" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;del</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/del&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Marks a deleted section of content. This element can also be used as <i>inline</i>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="div"></span><span class="anchor" id="div_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Logical division" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;div</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/div&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Span_and_div" title="Span and div">Span and div</a></div>\n<dl><dd>A block-level logical division. A generic element with no semantic meaning used to distinguish a document section, usually for purposes such as presentation or behavior controlled by <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">style sheets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">DOM</a> calls.</dd>\n<dd>Proposed in the <a href="#HTML30">HTML 3.0 Drafts</a>; <b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="figure"></span><span class="anchor" id="figure_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Figure" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;figure</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/figure&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used to group images and captions, along with <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;figcaption&gt;</code>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="figcaption"></span><span class="anchor" id="figcaption_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Figure Caption" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;figcaption</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/figcaption&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A caption for an image. Always placed inside the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;figure&gt;</code> element.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="header"></span><span class="anchor" id="footer_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Footer" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;footer</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/footer&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used for document footers. These might contain author or copyright information, or links to other pages.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="header"></span><span class="anchor" id="header_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Header" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;header</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/header&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used for document headers. These typically contain content introducing the page.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="hr"></span><span class="anchor" id="hr_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Thematic break" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;hr</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A thematic break (originally: horizontal rule). Presentational rules can be drawn with style sheets.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="ins"></span><span class="anchor" id="ins_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Inserted Section" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;ins</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/ins&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Marks a section of inserted content. This element can also be used as <i>inline</i>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="main"></span><span class="anchor" id="main_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Main Content" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;main</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/main&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Contains the main content of a document.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML 5.1</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="menu"></span><span class="anchor" id="menu_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Menu" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;menu</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/menu&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>HTML 2.0: A menu listing.
