Should be more compact than a <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;ul&gt;</code> list.</dd>\n<dd><code>MENU</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a>; <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>; then redefined in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>, but removed in HTML 5.2.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="nav"></span><span class="anchor" id="nav_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Navigation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;nav</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/nav&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used in navigational sections of articles (areas of webpages which contain links to other webpages).</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="noscript"></span><span class="anchor" id="noscript_tag"></span><code class="html" title="JavaScript Fallback" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;noscript</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/noscript&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Replacement content for scripts. Unlike <b>script</b> this can only be used as a block-level element.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="pre"></span><span class="anchor" id="pre_tag"></span><code class="html" title="PreFormatted Text" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;pre</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/pre&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><i>Pre-formatted</i> text. Text within this element is typically displayed in a <a href="/wiki/Non-proportional_font" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-proportional font">non-proportional font</a> exactly as it is laid out in the file (see <a href="/wiki/ASCII_art" title="ASCII art">ASCII art</a>). Whereas browsers ignore <a href="/wiki/Whitespace_(computer_science)" class="mw-redirect" title="Whitespace (computer science)">white-space</a> for other HTML elements, in <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;pre&gt;...&lt;&#47;pre&gt;</code>, white-space should be rendered as authored. (With the CSS properties: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">white-space</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">pre</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="k">font-family</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">monospace</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>, other elements can be presented in the same way.)  This element can contain any inline element except: <a href="#image"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;image&gt;</code></a>, <a href="#object"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;object&gt;</code></a>, <a href="#big"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;big&gt;</code></a>, <a href="#small"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;small&gt;</code></a>, <a href="#sup"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;sup&gt;</code></a>, and <a href="#sub"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;sub&gt;...&lt;&#47;sub&gt;</code></a>.</dd>\n<dd><code>PRE</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="section"></span><span class="anchor" id="section_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Section" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;section</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/section&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Used for generic sections of a document. This is different from <a href="#div"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;div&gt;</code></a> in that it is only used to contain sections of a page, which the W3C defines as a group of content with a similar theme.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="script"></span><span class="anchor" id="script_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Script" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;script</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/script&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Places a script in the document. Also usable in the head and in inline contexts.  It may be used as <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&#32;&#47;&gt;</code> with a <code>src</code> attribute to supply a URL from which to load the script, or used as <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&gt;...&lt;&#47;script&gt;</code> around embedded script content.\n<dl><dd><strong>Note:</strong> <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;script&gt;</code> is not itself either a block or inline element; by itself it should not display at all, but it can contain instructions to dynamically generate either both block or inline content.</dd></dl></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inline_elements">Inline elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Inline elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Inline elements cannot be placed directly inside the <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">body</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> element; they must be wholly nested within block-level elements.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Anchor">Anchor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Anchor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="a"></span><span class="anchor" id="a_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Anchor" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;a</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/a&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>An anchor element is called an anchor because web designers can use it to "anchor" a URL to some text on a web page. When users view the web page in a browser, they can click the text to activate the link and visit the page whose URL is in the link.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd>In HTML, an <i>anchor</i> can be either the <i>origin</i> (the <a href="/wiki/Anchor_text" title="Anchor text">anchor text</a>) or the <i>target</i> (destination) end of a <a href="/wiki/Hyperlink" title="Hyperlink">hyperlink</a>.</dd>\n<dd>With the attribute <code>href</code>,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the anchor becomes a hyperlink to either another part of the document or another resource (e.g. a webpage) using an external <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniform Resource Locator">URL</a>. Alternatively (and sometimes concurrently), with the <code>name</code> or <code>id</code> <a href="/wiki/HTML_attributes" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML attributes">HTML attributes</a> set, the element becomes a link target. A <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniform Resource Locator">Uniform Resource Locator</a> (URL) can link to this target via a <a href="/wiki/Fragment_identifier" class="mw-redirect" title="Fragment identifier">fragment identifier</a>. In HTML5, any element can now be made into a target by using the <code>id</code> attribute,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> so using <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">a</span> <span class="na">name</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;foo&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>...<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">a</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> is not necessary, although this way of adding anchors continues to work.</dd>\n<dd>To illustrate: the header of a table of contents section on <samp>example.com</samp>\'s homepage could be turned into a target by writing\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">h2</span><span class="p">&gt;&lt;</span><span class="nt">a</span> <span class="na">name</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;contents&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>Table of contents<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">a</span><span class="p">&gt;&lt;/</span><span class="nt">h2</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>Continuing with this example, now that the section has been marked up as a target, it can be referred to from external sites with a link like\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">a</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;http://example.com#contents&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>see contents<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">a</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>or with a link on the same page like:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">a</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;#contents&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>contents, above<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">a</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>The attribute <code>title</code> may be set to give brief information about the link:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">a</span> <span class="na">href</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;URL&quot;</span> <span class="na">title</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;additional information&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>link text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">a</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd>In most graphical browsers, when the cursor hovers over a link, the cursor changes into a hand with an extended index finger and the <code>title</code> value is displayed in a <a href="/wiki/Tooltip" title="Tooltip">tooltip</a> or in some other manner. Some browsers render <a href="/wiki/Alt_attribute" title="Alt attribute">alt text</a> the same way, although this is not what the specification calls for.</dd>\n<dd><code>A</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLTAGS">HTML Tags</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current</dd></dl>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Phrase_elements">Phrase elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Phrase elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Phrase elements are used for marking up phrases and adding structure or semantic meaning to text fragments. For example, the <code>&lt;em&gt;</code> and <code>&lt;strong&gt;</code> tags can be used for adding emphasis to text.\n</p>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="abbr"></span><span class="anchor" id="abbr_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Abbreviation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;abbr</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/abbr&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Marks an <a href="/wiki/Abbreviation" title="Abbreviation">abbreviation</a>, and can make the full form available:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">abbr</span> <span class="na">title</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;abbreviation&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>abbr.<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">abbr</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="acronym"></span><span class="anchor" id="acronym_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Acronym" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;acronym</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/acronym&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Similar to the <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">abbr</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> element, but marks an <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronym</a>:\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">acronym</span> <span class="na">title</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;Hyper-Text Mark-up Language&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>HTML<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">acronym</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd></dl></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current, <b>not supported</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>. Recommended replacement is the <code>abbr</code> tag.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="dfn"></span><span class="anchor" id="dfn_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Definition" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;dfn</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/dfn&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Inline definition of a single term.</dd>\n<dd><code>DFN</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was fully <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="em"></span><span class="anchor" id="em_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Emphasis" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;em</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/em&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><i>Emphasis</i> (conventionally displayed in italics)</dd>\n<dd><code>EM</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="strong"></span><span class="anchor" id="strong_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Importance" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;strong</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/strong&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><b>importance</b>; originally strong emphasis (conventionally displayed bold).</dd>\n<dd>An <a href="/wiki/Voice_browser" title="Voice browser">aural user agent</a> may use different voices for emphasis.</dd>\n<dd><code>STRONG</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current, redefined in HTML5.</dd></dl>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Computer_phrase_elements">Computer phrase elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Computer phrase elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>These elements are useful primarily for documenting computer code development and user interaction through differentiation of source code (<code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">code</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code>), variables (<code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code>), user input (<code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">kbd</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code>), and terminal or other output (<code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">samp</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code>).\n</p><p><span class="anchor" id="code"></span><span class="anchor" id="code_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Sourcecode" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;code</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/code&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A code snippet (<code>code example</code>). Conventionally rendered in a mono-space font.</dd>\n<dd><code>CODE</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="kbd"></span><span class="anchor" id="kbd_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Keyboard" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;kbd</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/kbd&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Keyboard \xe2\x80\x93 text to be entered by the user (<kbd>kbd example</kbd>).</dd>\n<dd><code>KBD</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="samp"></span><span class="anchor" id="samp_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Sample" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;samp</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/samp&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Sample output \xe2\x80\x93 from a program or script: (<samp>samp example</samp>).</dd>\n<dd><code>SAMP</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="var"></span><span class="anchor" id="var_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Variable" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;var</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/var&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Variable (<var>var example</var>).</dd>\n<dd><code>VAR</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Presentation">Presentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Presentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>\n<p>As visual presentational markup only applies directly to visual browsers, its use is discouraged. Style sheets should be used instead. Several of these elements are deprecated or invalid in HTML 4 / XHTML 1.0, and the remainder are invalid in the current draft of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.w3.org/TR/2005/WD-xhtml2-20050527/">XHTML 2.0</a>. The current draft of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20150801133040/http://www.w3.org/TR/html5/text-level-semantics.html">HTML5</a>, however, re-includes <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;s&gt;</code>, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;u&gt;</code>, and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;small&gt;</code>, assigning new semantic meaning to each. In an <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> document, the use of these elements is no longer discouraged, provided that it is semantically correct.\n</p><p><span class="anchor" id="b"></span><span class="anchor" id="b_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Keyword" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;b</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/b&gt;</b>\n</code> \n</p>\n<dl><dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, set font to <b>boldface</b> where possible. Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-weight</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">bold</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>. The <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;strong&gt;</code> element usually has the same effect in visual browsers, as well as having more semantic meaning, under <a href="/wiki/HTML_4.01" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4.01">HTML 4.01</a>.</dd>\n<dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, however, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;b&gt;</code> has its own meaning, distinct from that of <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;strong&gt;</code>. It denotes "text to which attention is being drawn for utilitarian purposes without conveying any extra importance and with no implication of an alternate voice or mood."<sup id="cite_ref-html5-b-element_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-b-element-38">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><code>B</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current, redefined in HTML5.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="i"></span><span class="anchor" id="i_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Alternate voice" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;i</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/i&gt;</b>\n</code> \n</p>\n<dl><dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, set font to <i>italic</i> where possible. Equivalent <a href="/wiki/CSS" title="CSS">CSS</a>: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-style</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">italic</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>. Using <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;em&gt;...&lt;&#47;em&gt;</code> has the same visual effect in most browsers, as well as having a semantic meaning as <i>emphasis</i>, under <a href="/wiki/HTML_4.01" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4.01">HTML 4.01</a>. (Purely typographic italics have many non-emphasis purposes, as HTML 5 more explicitly recognized.)</dd>\n<dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, however, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;i&gt;</code> has its own semantic meaning, distinct from that of <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;em&gt;</code>. It denotes "a different quality of text" or "an alternative voice or mood "e.g., a thought, a ship name, a <a href="/wiki/Binomial_nomenclature" title="Binomial nomenclature">binary species name</a>, a foreign-language phrase, etc."<sup id="cite_ref-html5-i-element_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-i-element-39">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><code>I</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current, redefined in HTML5.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="u"></span><span class="anchor" id="u_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Unarticulated annotation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;u</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/u&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, <u>underlined</u> text. Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">text-decoration</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">underline</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>. Deprecated in <a href="/wiki/HTML_4.01" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4.01">HTML 4.01</a>. Restored in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd>\n<dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;u&gt;</code> element denotes "a span of text with an unarticulated, though explicitly rendered, non-textual annotation, such as labelling the text as being a proper name in Chinese text (a Chinese proper name mark), or labelling the text as being misspelt."  The <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a> specification reminds developers that other elements are almost always more appropriate than <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;u&gt;</code> and admonishes designers not to use underlined text where it could be confused for a hyper-link.<sup id="cite_ref-html5-u-element_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-u-element-40">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><code>U</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a> but was <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a> and was <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>. <b>Reintroduced</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="small"></span><span class="anchor" id="small_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Side comment" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;small</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/small&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, decreased font size (<small>smaller</small> text). Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-size</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">smaller</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></dd>\n<dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;small&gt;</code> element denotes "side comments such as small print."<sup id="cite_ref-html5-small-element_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-small-element-41">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  This has caused some confusion with the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<a href="#aside">aside</a>&gt;...&lt;&#47;<a href="#aside">aside</a>&gt;</code> element.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="s"></span><span class="anchor" id="s_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Inacurrate text" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;s</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/s&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML_4" class="mw-redirect" title="HTML 4">HTML 4</a>, indicated strike-through text (<s>Strikethrough</s>) and was equivalent to <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;strike&gt;</code>.</dd>\n<dd>In <a href="/wiki/HTML5" title="HTML5">HTML5</a>, the <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;s&gt;</code> element denotes information that is "no longer accurate or no longer relevant", and is not to be confused with <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;del&gt;</code>, which indicates removal/deletion.<sup id="cite_ref-html5-s-element_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-s-element-42">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>\n<dd><code>S</code> was <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a> (having not appeared in any previous standard), and was <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>. <b>Reintroduced</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>, which instead deprecated <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;strike&gt;</code>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="big"></span><span class="anchor" id="big_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Big" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;big</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/big&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Increased font size (<big>bigger</big> text). Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-size</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">larger</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; <b>not supported</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="strike"></span><span class="anchor" id="strike_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Strikethrough" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;strike</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/strike&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Strike-through text (<s>Strikethrough</s>),  (Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">text-decoration</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">line-through</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>)</dd>\n<dd><code>STRIKE</code> was standardized in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a>; <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="tt"></span><span class="anchor" id="tt_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Teletype" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;tt</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/tt&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><a href="/wiki/Non-proportional_font" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-proportional font">Fixed-width</a> font (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886049734">.mw-parser-output .monospaced{font-family:monospace,monospace}</style><span class="monospaced">typewriter-like</span>), also known as <a href="/wiki/Teleprinter" title="Teleprinter">teletype</a>, thus "tt". (Equivalent CSS: <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-family</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">monospace</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code>)</dd>\n<dd><code>TT</code> existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; not supported<sup id="cite_ref-html5-tt-not-supported_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-tt-not-supported-43">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> in HTML5. Possible replacements: <a href="#kbd"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;kbd&gt;</code></a> for marking user input, <a href="#var"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;var&gt;</code></a> for variables (usually rendered italic, and not with a change to monospace), <a href="#code"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;code&gt;</code></a> for source code, <a href="#samp"><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;samp&gt;</code></a> for output.<sup id="cite_ref-html5-tt-not-supported_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-html5-tt-not-supported-43">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="font"></span><span class="anchor" id="font_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Teletype" style="font-size:116%;"><del style="color:grey;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;font</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/font&gt;</b></del> <b>(deprecated)</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="err">[</span><span class="na">color</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&lt;var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>color<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>] [size=<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>size<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>] [face=<span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>face<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">var</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>]&gt;...<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code></dd>\n<dd>Can specify the font color with the <code>color</code> attribute (note the American spelling), typeface with the <code>face</code> attribute, and absolute or relative size with the <code>size</code> attribute.</dd>\n<dd>Examples (all uses are deprecated, use CSS equivalents if possible):\n<ol><li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">color</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;green&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> creates <span style="color:green;">green text</span>.</li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">color</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;#114499&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> creates <span style="color:#149;">text with <a href="/wiki/Hex_triplet" class="mw-redirect" title="Hex triplet">hexadecimal color</a> #114499</span>.</li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">size</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;4&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> creates <span style="font-size:140%;">text</span> with size 4. Sizes are from 1 to 7. The standard size is 3, unless otherwise specified in the &lt;body&gt; or other tags.</li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">size</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;+1&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> creates <span style="font-size:125%;">text with size 1 bigger than the standard.</span> <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">size</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;-1&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> is opposite.</li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">face</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;Courier&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span>text<span class="p">&lt;/</span><span class="nt">font</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> makes <span style="font-family:Courier;">text</span> with Courier font.</li></ol></dd>\n<dd>Equivalent CSS for font attributes:\n<ul><li><code class="mw-highlight" dir="rtl"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">size</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">"<var>N</var>"</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> corresponds to <code class="mw-highlight" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span><span class="nb">font-size</span><span class="o" style="color: #666;">:</span> <span class="nb"><var>Y</var><var>units</var></span><span class="p">}</span></code> (the HTML specification does not define the relationship between size <var>N</var> and unit-size <var>Y</var>, nor does it define a unit).</li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">color</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;red&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> corresponds to <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">color</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="kc">red</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code></li>\n<li><code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-html mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">&lt;</span><span class="nt">font</span> <span class="na">face</span><span class="o">=</span><span class="s">&quot;Times New Roman&quot;</span><span class="p">&gt;</span></code> corresponds to <code class="mw-highlight mw-highlight-lang-css mw-content-ltr" id="" style="" dir="ltr"><span class="p">{</span> <span class="k">font-family</span><span class="p">:</span> <span class="s1">&#39;Times New Roman&#39;</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="n">Times</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="kc">serif</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="p">}</span></code> \xe2\x80\x93 CSS supports a <a href="/w/index.php?title=Font_stack&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Font stack (page does not exist)">font stack</a>, of two or more alternative fonts.</li></ul></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML32">HTML 3.2</a>; <b>deprecated</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Transitional</a>; <b>invalid</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0 Strict</a>. Not part of HTML5.</dd></dl>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Span">Span</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Span">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="span"></span><span class="anchor" id="span_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Span" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;span</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/span&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Span_and_div" title="Span and div">Span and div</a></div>\n<dl><dd>An inline logical division. A generic element with no semantic meaning used to distinguish a document section, usually for purposes such as presentation or behavior controlled by <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">style sheets</a> or <a href="/wiki/Document_Object_Model" title="Document Object Model">DOM</a> calls.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_inline_elements">Other inline elements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=HTML_element&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other inline elements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="br"></span><span class="anchor" id="br_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Line Break" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;br</b><b style="color:#006633">&#160;/&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A forced line break.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="bdi"></span><span class="anchor" id="bdi_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Bidirectional Isolation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;bdi</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/bdi&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Isolates an inline section of text that may be formatted in a different direction from other text outside of it, such as user-generated content with unknown directionality.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="bdo"></span><span class="anchor" id="bdo_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Bidirectional Override" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;bdo</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/bdo&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Marks an inline section of text in which the reading direction is the opposite from that of the parent element.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="cite"></span><span class="anchor" id="cite_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Citation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;cite</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/cite&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>A citation or a reference for a quote or statement in the document.</dd>\n<dd>CITE existed in <i><a href="#HTMLDRAFT12">HTML Internet Draft 1.2</a></i>, and was <b>standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML20">HTML 2.0</a>; still current.</dd>\n<dd><i>Note:</i> The HTML 5 specifications have been confusingly <a href="/wiki/Fork_(software_development)" title="Fork (software development)">forked</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-finalars_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finalars-44">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> including with regard to this element. In HTML 4 and earlier, <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;cite&gt;</code> was for "a citation or a reference to other sources" without any particular limitations or requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/W3C" class="mw-redirect" title="W3C">W3C</a> HTML 5 spec uses a refinement of this idea, reflecting how the element has historically been used, but now requiring that it contain (but not be limited to) at least one of "the title of the work or the name of the author (person, people or organization) or an URL reference, or a reference in abbreviated form as per the conventions used for the addition of citation metadata."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> But the WHATWG spec only permits the element to be used around the title of a work.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>  The W3C specs began with the broader definition, then switched to the very narrow one after WHATWG made this change. However, W3C reverted their own change in 2012, in response to negative developer-community feedback; the element was in broadly-deployed use with the broader scope, e.g., various blog and forum platforms wrap commenters\' IDs and e-mail addresses in <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;cite&gt;...&lt;&#47;cite&gt;</code>, and people using the element for bibliographic citations were (and still are) routinely wrapping each entire citation in this element.</dd>\n<dd>Another problem with the element is that WHATWG recommends that it be italicized by default (thus almost all browsers do so), because it (in their view) is only for publication titles. By convention, however, only certain kinds of titles actually take italics, while others are expected to be put in quotation marks, and standards may actually vary by publishing context and language. Consequently, many website authors and admins use a site-wide stylesheet to undo this element\'s auto-italics.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="data"></span><span class="anchor" id="data_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Data" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;data</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/data&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Links inline content with a machine-readable translation.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="del"></span><span class="anchor" id="del_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Deleted" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;del</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/del&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Deleted text. Typically rendered as a <a href="/wiki/Strikethrough" title="Strikethrough">strikethrough</a>: <del>Deleted text.</del></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="ins"></span><span class="anchor" id="ins_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Inserted" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;ins</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/ins&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Inserted text. Often used to mark up replacement text for material struck with <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;del&gt;</code> or <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;s&gt;</code>. Typically rendered <a href="/wiki/Underline" class="mw-redirect" title="Underline">underlined</a>: <ins>Inserted text.</ins></dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd>\n<dd>Both <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;ins&gt;</code> and <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;del&gt;</code> elements may also be used as block elements: containing other block and inline elements. However, these elements must still remain wholly within their parent element to maintain a well-formed HTML document. For example, deleting text from the middle of one paragraph across several other paragraphs and ending in a final paragraph would need to use three separate <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;del&gt;</code> elements. Two <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;del&gt;</code> elements would be required as inline elements to indicate the deletion of text in the first and last paragraphs, and a third, used as a block element, to indicate the deletion in the intervening paragraphs.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="mark"></span><span class="anchor" id="mark_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Mark" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;mark</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/mark&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Produces text that looks <mark>like this</mark>. Intended for highlighting relevant text in a quotation.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.</dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="q"></span><span class="anchor" id="q_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Quote" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;q</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/q&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>An inline quotation (for block level quotation see <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;<a href="#blockquote">blockquote</a>&gt;</code>). Quote elements may be nested.</dd>\n<dd><code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;q&gt;</code> <em>should</em> automatically generate quotation marks in conjunction with style sheets. Practical concerns due to browser non-compliance may force authors to find workarounds.</dd>\n<dd>The <code>cite</code> attribute gives the source, and must be a fully qualified <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Identifier" title="Uniform Resource Identifier">URI</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML401">HTML 4.0</a>; still current.</dd>\n<dd><strong>Note:</strong> Lengthy inline quotations may be displayed as indented blocks (as <code>block-quote</code>) using style sheets. For example, with a suitable CSS rule associated with <code>q.lengthy</code>: <code class="nowrap" style="">&lt;q&gt;Lengthy quote here.&lt;&#47;q &gt;</code></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="rb"></span><span class="anchor" id="rb_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ruby Annotation Base" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;rb</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/rb&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Represents the base component of a <a href="/wiki/Ruby_character" title="Ruby character">ruby annotation</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="rp"></span><span class="anchor" id="rp_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ruby Fallback Parenthesis" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;rp</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/rp&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Provides fallback parenthesis for browsers lacking <a href="/wiki/Ruby_character" title="Ruby character">ruby annotation</a> support.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="rt"></span><span class="anchor" id="rt_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ruby Annotation Pronunciation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;rt</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/rt&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Indicates pronunciation for a character in a <a href="/wiki/Ruby_character" title="Ruby character">ruby annotation</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="rtc"></span><span class="anchor" id="rtc_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ruby Semantic Annotation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;rtc</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/rtc&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Semantic annotations for a <a href="/wiki/Ruby_character" title="Ruby character">ruby annotation</a>.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="ruby"></span><span class="anchor" id="ruby_tag"></span><code class="html" title="Ruby Annotation" style="font-size:116%;"><b style="color:#006633">&lt;ruby</b><b style="color:#006633">&gt;</b>...<b style="color:#006633">&lt;/ruby&gt;</b>\n</code>\n</p>\n<dl><dd>Represents a <a href="/wiki/Ruby_character" title="Ruby character">ruby annotation</a> for showing the pronunciation of East Asian characters.</dd>\n<dd><b>Standardized</b> in <a href="#HTML5">HTML5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="anchor" id="script"></span><span class="anchor" id="script_tag"></span><code class="html"
